B008I3R2VG|4.0|3 and a 1/2 stars if I could give it that.<br />Battle Born has had 6 days of heavy playing at my home, work and car and each day has seen my review become slightly more favourable. Which is good as it was going to be a `killer' at first.<br /><br />On the first few listens to Battle Born my impressions were:<br />Disappointment<br />Not what I was expecting or hoping for<br />Synths for synths sake?<br />Where are the guitars?<br />Where's the power? What's up with these ballads? THE KILLERS DON'T DO BALLADS!!!<br />Where are the hooks and melodies?<br />Where's this `ace' that Brandon Flowers said he saved from his solo album?<br />Who let U2 in the room?<br />The first positive I picked up on is how good BF's voice sounds here. He's certainly improved since his Sam's Town delusions of grandeur.<br /><br />So it's fair to say that I WAS NOT IMPRESSED with Battle Born on its early listenings. My opinion has improved somewhat but I'm still not happy. It's not an album of hooks and melodies as was Day and Age. The power of Sam's Town is missing and the edge of Hot Fuss is non-existent.<br /><br />I absolutely love Runaways. I think it's one of the best songs they've done. It's the only standout here though. I was hoping The K's would take everything they've done in the past and create their own identity but all they've done here is made themselves sound like other bands.<br /><br />When you get a new album you have a listen. Then another one and a track (other than the single(s) you know) stands out for you. You give that one track some extra listening. You feel good and then another track will standout and so forth and the rest of the album builds around those stand outs. On listening to this one though, that didn't happen for me.<br /><br />On past albums, synths have played a big part but here, they've overdone, generic and pointless. They don't add to most songs but are present in almost all of them.<br /><br />On a plus, there's nothing really bad here. It's perhaps their most consistent album to date. That's also its problem. Each song blends with the next and nothing grabs you. No one song lets the rest down but other than Runaways, nothing else truly rises to the challenge.<br /><br />It's an album of interesting sounding verses but in many cases, the chorus lets the song down by being clichÃ©d or generic. An album that perhaps belongs in the 80's where many of these sounds seem to be from.<br /><br />As for the songs:<br />4/5 - Flesh And Bone is one of the stronger tracks. Catchy and a good mix of synth and rock. My kids love this one too.<br />5/5 - Runaways is brilliant, one of their best ever.<br />4/5 - The Way It Was is OK. It's pretty lightweight though. It lies between rock and power ballad and is lacking something. Wasn't overly fussed on it until the last fading: \\"maybe a thief stole your heart' struck a chord with me.<br />3/5 - Here With me reminds me of the REO Speedwagon song of the same name. The first of three ballads. Not fussed on this 80's sounding power ballad. I skip this track more than any other.<br />3/5 - A Matter Of Time is a reasonable song with a bad chorus.<br />4/5 - Deadlines And Commitments at first sounded like bad 80's movie soundtrack song to me but has grown on me and is one of my favourite tracks. Reminds me a bit Robert Palmer.<br />3.5/5 - Miss Atomic Bomb is U2. It's an OK song and one of the better ones but it just sounds like them trying to sound like U2. And the line: \\"You're gonna miss me when I'm gone\\". C'mon!! be original!!<br />3/5 - The Rising Tide borders on annoying. It's OK and I'm not really sure why I feel this way about it but I skip this one often. I hope, in time, I can like this one more. More mid-tempo over-synthed fare.<br />3/5 - Heart Of A Girl is more U2. The second ballad. It's OK I guess but would be better if, again, it wasn't a plain U2 rip off - and maybe released in the 90's. And \\"a ripple in the water\\" makes me cringe. Nice message though and is almost an OK track.<br />4/5 - From Here On Out is finally some fun. Perhaps better suited on BF's solo but a nice track. At leasts it's up-tempo!!<br />3/5 - Be Still features a... a.... a.. DRUM MACHINE!!! What? You have a drummer!! Use him. You don't use a drum machine!!! On the plus side, this one is sung very well. Maybe the pick of the ballads - the ballads that don't belong on a Killers album. \\"Is this real or just a dream?\\" - more original writing.<br />4/5 Battle Born hooray!! Finally some power. Good track this one and finally some semblance of the previous Killer sound. It's what the rest of the album should be like. Something to get excited about here but, oh dear, the albums over.....<br /><br />The bonus tracks are OK - there are five on my copy. Carry Me Home sounds like a boring Day & Age throwaway. Prize Fighter is a good, fun song and could probably find its way onto the album in lieu of one of the ballads. The remixes: (Flesh and Bone and Runaways) are what rock remixes are - pointless exercises that retract from the original. The Be Still alternative cut is an interesting one. It loses the drum machine and allows Ronnie to participate. It won't go as far to say it's better (because I think both versions could do with some stripping down) but at least there's no drum machine.<br /><br />My favourite Killers album to date has been Day & Age. This new album ranks last in their four albums and also rates behind Brandon Flowers' solo effort - which I also love.<br /><br />I will go as far to say that Battle Born is my biggest musical disappointment for over a decade. Perhaps the hiatus has seen the boys use their best material for their solo stuff and what's presented here has been left a little thin?<br /><br />I still love The Killers. this one 'slight' mis-step doens't erase the countless hours of enjoyment they've brought me over the past 8 years. Here's hoping in time I'll be able to come back, admit I was wrong, retract this review and rewrite a positive one......
B001229W22|5.0|Whenever an album (or any piece of media, for that matter) reaches a certain level of cultural and critical fame, there's a risk of backlash from the listening public.  Expectations have been set very high coming in, and new listeners are not likely to be forgiving if the album falls short, no matter how unattainable what was promised might be.  It seems being overrated is a far worse crime than being merely of poor quality.<br /><br /> This is the challenge that Master of Puppets finds itself in.  Metallica's third album has been widely hailed not only as a brilliant achievement, but a clear contender for the title of greatest metal album ever composed.  That's no small claim, and whether or not it holds up in the end, expectations are still going to be incredibly high.<br /><br /> And I have a hard time believing that it doesn't meet them.  Giving this record a listen for what may be the hundredth time, it's a testament to Metallica's compositional prowess how fresh it still sounds.  There's a bit of magic in the performance; the band is angry, unforgiving, and inspired, and it shows throughout the fifty-some minute running time.  Hetfield gives his definitive performance here, with his melodic snarl melding perfectly with Kirk Hammet's harsh, oft-chugging guitar work.  Cliff Burton bass is as good as the band has ever been, and Lars... well... he can hit drums somewhat competently, I suppose.  Every song is given the treatment it deserves here, from the colossal \\"Battery\\" to the proggy instrumental \\"Orion\\".<br /><br /> The typical Metallica album layout is here, and refined to perfection.  \\"Battery\\" is an up-tempo thrasher hard enough to break your teeth on, but still catchy enough to follow from the first listen.  \\"Master of Puppets\\" and \\"Disposable Heroes\\" are both epics, with some of the best solos of Kirk Hammet's career.  \\"Welcome Home (Sanitarium)\\" is a great improvement on the similarly-styled \\"Fade to Black\\" from [[ASIN:B000002H2H Ride the Lightning]], with a light, melodic first half, and a heavy, instrumental second half.  \\"The Thing That Should Not Be\\" is another Lovecraft-inspired bit of horror; it may have a plodding pace, but it fits the subject matter perfectly.  \\"Orion\\" is the instrumental; Metallica seemed to be going with a progressive feel for this one - it strikes me as vaguely Opeth-ian, which is a very good thing.  With light, atmospheric work blending with the heavier riffs and organic solos, this one is a real winner.  Some songs, such as \\"Leper Messiah\\" are admittedly weaker than the rest, but that just means the bar is set to \\"high\\" rather than \\"very high\\".<br /><br /> Master of Puppets is undoubtedly required listening, and I would recommend getting any non-metal friends around to listen as well.  You may not win any converts, but it is textbook metal, and will give them a better idea than anything of what the genre is about.<br /><br /> Best metal album ever?  Maybe.<br /> One you'll still be listening to years from now?  Definitely.th a light, melodic first half, and a heavy, instrumental second half.  \\"The Thing That Should Not Be\\" is another Lovecraft-inspired bit of horror; it may have a plodding pace, but it fits the subject matter perfectly.  \\"Orion\\" is the instrumental; Metallica seemed to be going with a progressive feel for this one - it strikes me as vaguely Opeth-ian, which is a very good thing.  With light, atmospheric work blending with the heavier riffs and organic solos, this one is a real winner.  Some songs, such as \\"Leper Messiah\\" are admittedly weaker than the rest, but that just means the bar is set to \\"high\\" rather than \\"very high\\".<br /><br /> Master of Puppets is undoubtedly required listening, and I would recommend getting any non-metal friends around to listen as well.  You may not win any converts, but it is textbook metal, and will give them a better idea than anything of what the genre is about.<br /><br /> Best metal album ever?  Maybe.<br /> One you'll still be listening to years from now?  Definitely.

1439153663|5.0|I saw this book on a reading site and became interested after reading the editorial review and book description.  Even though it was a first book by a new author, I took a chance and ordered it from Amazon. Wow, am I glad I did!  This story ranks among the very best of books I've read, and I've read a LOT of books.  I always enjoy a story about Southern plantations, but this book tells the story from the slaves point of view.  The author grabs your attention from the very first page, and I was riveted throughout the entire book (I finished it in 2 days).  As you might expect, this is not a light read.  All of the characters experience heartbreak and horrors, they feel trapped in their circumstances. I felt I got to know the characters and felt their pain and emotional turmoil.  This book gives the reader a new appreciation for what it was actually like to be a slave in the south.  I had toured a plantation when we visited South Carolina several years ago and recalled the actual slave cabins I saw there and how very small they were.  It was easy to imagine the characters from this story living in those cramped, sparse quarters.<br /><br />If you like historical fiction and are looking for a book that will both teach you something and touch your heart, this is it. This book will stay with you for years to come; I know it affected me deeply. Excellent first book by a new author - I can't wait for her next one!
B0071BGOJC|4.0|Winter of the World is volume 2 of a saga covering all of the 20th century, focusing on four interrelated families: American, British, German and Russian. Follett has done a commendable job of juggling these characters using their personal stories to lead the reader (in this volume) through the major historical events of an era running from 1933 to 1949 (the rise of Nazism to the beginning of the Cold War).<br />His huge cast of characters is made up of plastic, credible humans, many of whom are capable of growing into the situations thrust upon them, and by situations that are sometimes almost too horrible for words - but are nonetheless borne out by history. Yes, these things actually happened!<br />Follett leads us through the burning of the Reichstag, the Spanish civil war, Hitler's annexation of Czechoslovakia and Poland, the Soviet-German non-aggression pact, Stalin's mistrust of his own espionage agents and the resulting disasters, the Battle of Britain, etc. and manages to make it all close and personal! Missing however (the reason I withheld the 5th star) are the heroic rescue effort at Dunkirk, the saturation bombings (fire bombings) of places like Guernica, Dresden and Hamburg and especially, the siege of Leningrad! I'm not sure how an 872 day siege with its tremendous loss of life and unimaginable heroism escaped the author's notice. Granted, none of his characters were there and putting them there might have been difficult. But, to leave it unmentioned?<br />Clearly, covering the history of that period is an enormous project, but the enormity is no excuse for skipping events that are key to the memories the various nations involved ... the carnage that was D-Day was also brushed over lightly.<br />Critique notwithstanding, the book was fast-paced, exciting, and really hard to put down! I'm looking forward to the 3rd volume, but first I intend to re-read this one.

0525953728|4.0|Personally, I've been involved in the military community ever since I can remember. Both of my parents worked for the US military, I worked with the military, and have been supporting our military veterans in my own capacity for years. Thus, I wasn't much interested in reading a book that had a heavy emphasis on a mission that has yet to be declassified. I mean, how much can you learn about a case that is still heavily cloaked by the agencies?<br /><br />However, it peaked my interest when most of the one star reviews cited unethical disclosure and disclosures of classified information that could jeapordize our national security. I had to find out why the current administration and the CIA are contemplating on taking legal actions to censure this book; I had to see if this patriot had crossed the line that would turn him into a traitor instead. Funny, isn't it? For once, negative actions of these folks prompted me to purchase a book that I would not normally have pursued.<br /><br />I read the book in two days as soon as I received it.<br /><br />First of all, the book is divided into two major sections : pre OBL mission and the OBL mission.<br /><br />The first half of the book delved into the authors motivations and experiences prior to the operation. He detailed his initial exposure to the elite forces culture, the experiences of his youth, and his subequent pursuit of his carrer. It is in this section that readers might find his narrative a bit disorientating. This section is not written in strict chronological sequence; he bounces between episodes of his training with past reminesences of his youth. I found this section mildly interesting due to the absense of sensitive details of his training and missions; I fouund this section to be endearing due to the cohesiveness of his childhood experiences and those of his adult values. Nothing here can really be scrutinized for questionable content. It was simply the autobiographical section of the book.<br /><br />TheOBL mission took up the second half of the book. While I found this section to be an interesting read, the obvious lack of sensitive 'secrets' is what prompted me to write this review in the authors' defense. The author told the story from his personal experience without disclosing the mariad of details he could have exposed of the intelligence community and of the  peripheral operational components. He expressed only of his reactions and actions without exposing others that made the mission possible. The operational summary he had written in this book would be of common knowledge to anyone who simply delve into the subject and thus could not be construed 'sensitive' by any means.<br /><br />A few reviewers condemned the tidbits of political remarks the author related between his mates. The remarks were simply sarcastic exchanges that lighten moods rather than making political statements; similar remarks would have been made no matter who was in the white house. For that matter, any stressful work place would find similar jokes about management and bosses during their downtime.<br /><br />The author disclosed that his central motivation for writing this book was to, perhaps, motivate a future special forces operative to pursue this noble endeavor. For such, I felt he did a marvelous job. This book is engaging, patriotic, personalble while not being overbearing. It's not Shakespearean; it's not supposed to be. Trying to judge this book by literary standard is simply absurd. It is a young adult read that was well put together for its stated purpose!

The memory that stuck with me ever since, and whenever I read it again: this is a must-read comic book masterpiece. Permeated with his peculiar storytelling, Moore paints an interesting picture of how would the real world be if superheroes walked amongst ordinary people and its implications. In its several pages, you never get the sensation of being had. You don't get the feeling of having your precious time wasted. Based upon actual scientific facts, proving that Moore is for the comics what Kubrick was for the cinema, he sews an intricate web filled with suspense, in his unique way approaches the ethics of power and its consequences if applied by someone with the means and pragmatic enough to do it, and gives birth to one of the most hard-to-copy pieces of the genre. After the live action incarnation, I had to add the english version to my collection. I couldn't resist! Now I can read it in its original lexicon.

B008AS5UAO|5.0|The new recording of Mozart's DON GIOVANNI has been hyped and touted and finally it is here!  Incidentally, Ildebrando D'Arcangelo is in the current cast of this opera at the Los Angeles Opera opening this week so appetites are whetted. The audiences here were treated to Mariusz Kwiecien singing the role of Giovanni in the Los Angeles Philharmonic production this past spring under the direction of Gustavo Dudamel; he will be a tough act to follow.<br /><br />For all the drama that his recording engenders it is interesting to note that it is based on a concert performance in Baden-Baden in July 2011 with  Yannick N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin conducting the Mahler Chamber Orchestra.  His approach to the opera is lively but lacks a certain depth to make the truly dramatic scenes ring aw strongly as the lighter portions of the opera. He does however allow each of the vocalists to develop well-defined characters without superimposing tempi or mannerisms that would otherwise make this sound like a Singspiel.<br /><br />And what a cast this is!  The Don Giovanni of Ildebrando D'Arcangelo, the  sonorous bass baritone, is very dark and even in the lighter moments with Leporello he manages to always remind us of his darker side of his nature. Yes, his is a beautiful voice and he convinces us of his reputation as the lothario supreme.  But in the role of Leporello, Luca Pisaroni stands out as a baritone who will likely advance to the Giovanni role with a characterization and sound that is more completely well rounded- time for flirting as well as for evil doings. His contribution to this performance is exemplary.  The other men In this recording likewise hold forth on a very high level. Rolando Villazon as Don Ottavio sounds secure and if anything his once injured voice has a more burnished tone that is very appealing. Konstantin Wolff is a polished Masetto.<br /><br />The women are astonishingly well sung and for many it is their roles that make this recording unique.  Joyce DiDonato brings not only splendid technique in her wide range allows her to give equal beauty to both the high and low portions of Donna Elvira's role, but the personality she creates is totally credible. The tessitura of Elvira's arias has defeated many singers, being ungainly for most sopranos and high for most mezzo-sopranos who have attempted the role.  This is a role that Ms. DiDonato seems to have been born to sing and the gleam of her tone as she confidently moves from bottom to top of the voice is arresting.  As mentioned before, the stylishness with which she sings Mozart is splendid. Mojca Erdmann Gives Zerlina not only the beauty of a well schooled voice, but the snappiness of a completely conceived soubrette.  And as far as sheer beauty of voice and Mozartean sound and agility of singing Diana Damrau nearly steals the production with on of the finest Donna Anna on record. She has mastered the art of bel canto and thus is able to take greater liberties with embellishing her music than her colleagues.<br /><br />In all this is a splendid new DON GIOVANNI cast and the recording has so much going for it that the blemishes are minor.  Grady Harp, September 12s not only splendid technique in her wide range allows her to give equal beauty to both the high and low portions of Donna Elvira's role, but the personality she creates is totally credible. B008I3R2VG|5.0|Disclaimer: This is my favorite band of all time so please, take everything I say with a grain of salt. That said, I admit that though eventually I was able to find enjoyment from DAY & AGE I can understand why it got such criticism as it did. I love HOT FUSS but I consider SAM'S TOWN to be the essential album of The Killers. I have good news. Though BATTLE BORN may not be as good as SAM'S TOWN, it is definitely a worthy sequel. It's great to have the band back.<br /><br />BATTLE BORN is a \\"dustland fairytale\\" to the core. This is a complete and total \\"blue jean serenade\\" of layered, polished, and refined music. The production value is excellent but it is important to remember that The Killers can actually perform this live. This isn't just studio magic. This band is a premium act.<br /><br />BATTLE BORN is much more SAM'S TOWN than it is DAY & AGE but there is still some of that disco-glam-dance influence to be found. BATTLE BORN is primarily heartland rock, infused with a dose of country (a la Brandon's solo album FLAMINGO). It's an interesting blend and it's not for everyone. I know there are those who lament the band's departure from HOT FUSS but I personally appreciate the dynamic range of The Killers. I'm not going to discuss every song for once, just my absolute favorites. But enough introduction, on to the music!<br /><br />\\"Flesh and Bone\\" - At the moment this is my favorite track on BATTLE BORN. This is a rousing battle hymn if I've ever heard one. Brandon on synth and Dave on guitar are the driving force of the song but it is the lyrics that really give this song punch. I'd bet money that this is the next single released from the album.<br /><br />\\"Runaways\\" - This will always hold a special place in my heart as the first new song of the reunited Killers. From Ronnie's galloping percussion to the soaring vocals and reverberating guitar this track screams arena rock. This is a BIG song that is barely contained by the limitations of digital recording.<br /><br />\\"Matter of Time\\" - The way this track starts reminds me of HOT FUSS, with the heavier pace and the background vocals (\\"whoooa-ooo-oooo\\").  It's has a distinct \\"Somebody Told Me\\" flavor to it, with a hint of SAM'S TOWN. As another great arena rock song this will be fun to sing along to live.<br /><br />\\"Deadlines and Commitments\\" - I wasn't really digging this song at first. Like, at all. After listening to it a couple times it has really grown on me. At various times of the day I found myself singing, \\"If you should fall upon hard times...\\" An unexpected hit this one.<br /><br />\\"Miss Atomic Bomb\\" - I liked this one. And then I really listened to it. And then I fell in love. This is decent...until you realize that it is the prequel to \\"Mr. Brightside\\" and it totally blows your mind. This probably has some of the best lyrics of the entire album and in true Killers fashion it tells a beautiful, sad story. It sort of reminds me of \\"Dustland Fairytale\\" one of my all time favorites.<br /><br />`The Rising Tide\\" - There is some awkward lyrical delivery on this track, the first line for instance, \\"the streets of persuasion, are plated with gold, your heart's in the right place but you traveled down the wrong road...\\" But once you get past some of the unwieldly lines (think \\"Swallow It\\" from FLAMINGO) it really is a good song. Plus there is a wicked sweet guitar riff courtesy of Dave near the end.<br /><br />\\"From Here On Out\\" - This isn't heartland rock so much as it is country but you know what? I can dig it. This is also reminiscent of Brandon's solo album, kinda makes you want to throw on some cowboy boots and square dance.<br /><br />\\"Battle Born\\" - Here it is, the theme song of the album. It opens with ascending keyboard and guitar. This track is certainly an inspirational anthem. I love the guitar and drums but best of all is the vocals as Brandon reminds us all, we are battle born.<br /><br />Overall BATTLE BORN is a great album, just the return I have been waiting four years for. The Killers are back and in fine form. There are tracks that don't carry the same youthful enthusiasm and impressive scope that I so admire (\\"The Way it Was\\" and \\"Here With Me\\") and I can't stand \\"Heart of a Girl\\" but all in all this is a Grade A album. I highly recommend obtaining the two bonus tracks, \\"Carry Me Home\\" and especially \\"Prize Fighter.\\" If you are among The Victims rest easy, the band is back together and making music just as memorable as ever.iting four years for. I couldn't help but think as I read this that King doesn't even begin to scratch the surface of all of the implications of the butterfly effect and what would happen if one went back in time and interacted with even just one person. King seems to opt for the easy, predictable ending; I must say I half expected something a bit more twisted. Instead, his ending borders on the sweet and poignant, contributing to an overall feel good and more than satisfactory reading experience.

B000001Y2U|5.0|It's been at least a decade since I bought this album, after discovering Nine Inch Nails. Since that time I've traced back their influences, through Skinny Puppy, Einsteurzende Neubauten, Adam Ant, back to the grandaddies of them all, Suicide, Throbbing Gristle, David Bowie. I've heard everything the industrial genre has to offer and this album still sounds fresh in every way to my jaded ear.<br /><br />The first Manson albums reflect a combination of Trent Reznor's formidable production with the first big ideas of Marilyn himself. The musicians are talented, the songs are musically original, the production and sampling are first rate, the emotion and depth of the songs is impeccable.<br /><br />Marilyn spins this as a concept album with references to Nietzsche and Ayn Rand, about some character that is not himself, but the ruse is transparent. These songs are autobiographical in pornographic detail. Someone who has had a relationship with someone severely emotionally disturbed will relate painfully well to Tourniquet. Someone who has left a disgusting backwoods town to realize himself will have Man That You Fear as their anthem. Someone who has been stomped on in their quest for happiness and bootstraps themselves back up through the furious realization that their only savior is in the mirror will resonate with every second of The Reflecting God.<br /><br />There's a lot of unhealthy psychological baggage in here that Marilyn unpacks and analyzes in a very public way. Some of this is extremely cathartic. There will be times in your life that are hard, your eyes will open and you will see one of these songs in a new light, and realize that this man is another flawed but restless traveler, earnestly searching for answers.<br /><br />This is the best workout album.

B005J4TLN4|3.0|I wasn't expecting very much from this movie so I was a bit surprised that it got better as it went along. And I do enjoy the fact that films set in England cannot automatically rely on GUNS for all of the killing action. When the kids scatter to their apartments to get armed for the fight...........in the US they'd have assault weapons or at least a variety of hand guns. Here they must rely on baseball bats, swords, chains, gas filled (spoiler alert) super soakers, knives & yes, a few hand guns. The aliens were creepy & surreal -- like shaggy puppies with wicked fangs. And unlike most Alien movies, these critters are vulnerable & not that bright. Good at mindless killing but stoppable. I was surprised at the level of tension that was created in the various face-offs between monsters & kids, monsters & adults, kids and other badder kids, cops & everyone else. The opening sequence drags along too much but it sets the stage for the rest of the action. An interesting shout out to PBS style Nature shows too. Funny that. I did have a bit of a struggle with the cockney accent.........say what?!  But after awhile the dialogue wasn't really needed to enjoy the action. So really.....3 1/2 Stars overall. And yeah -- different rendering of \\"what if\\" by landing the Aliens in a crowded urban setting instead of a desert, ocean, small town or other more isolated setting. Good idea fairly well presented.
B000SEIDR0|2.0|\\"Omnivore's Dilemma\\" is my least favorite book by Pollan to date -- and, after reading this book, I'm not sure I'll attempt another of his in the future. My disappointment mostly comes from the extremely weak and cursory ending -- in fact, I wish I had stopped reading the book two-thirds of the way in. The sections comprising the first two-thirds of the book -- covering corn production and \\"grass farming\\" (i.e., animal farming) -- were both interesting and informative. The last section of the book was more personal, and held less interest for me. Here Pollan covers his personal experiences experimenting with vegetarianism, hunting for wild boar, and foraging for mushrooms. This all culminates into what he calls \\"the perfect meal\\" -- an entirely unrealistic and completely symbolic undertaking consisting of foraged and hunted foods.<br /><br />My main complaint is that Pollan's arguments against animal rights were superficial -- as someone familiar with issues surrounding animal rights, I feel that his treatment of the topic was very shallow. For this reason, I wish that he hadn't devoted an entire chapter to the topic, as he certainly didn't give it his due. Also, I found a few instances in this book that cited statistics that are incorrect.<br /><br />He ends the book with no real strong conclusions, except for perhaps \\"eat local\\". I really was expecting more.
